charyte werkys actyflyf boūde therto takyng prelacye tyme fulfyllyd hygher party charite ī contēplacyon god gostly thynges prayer medytacyons hadden charyte god euen crysten bothe affeccyō soule within also shewyng bodyly dedys withouten men yt contemplatyf fre fro al curys prelacye hadden ful charyte god euen cristen affeccyon soule ī outwarde shewynge hap mek ylit ye ful inwarde y• myȝt ne neded ne fyl hē shewe outwarde men y• prelacye also y• ho • temper •• men hadden full charyte affeccyon within also ī werkynge yt properly medled lyf bothe actyf contemplatyf lyf sothly suche man spyrytuell souereynte prelatis curatis ben ī temperel souereynte worldly lordes maysters holde medled lyf best behouely hem longe bounden therto y• fre bounden temperel ministracyō ne spyrytual hope lyfe contemplatyf alone yf myght come therto sothfastly best skedful medeful fayre worthy hem vse holde leue wylfully ony outwarde werkyng actyflyf yf grete nede grete releuyng comfortyng men eyther bodyes soules yf nede aske prayer instaunce elles byddyng souereyn hope gode shewe hē outwarde werkys actyflyf tyme helpynge euern crysten ¶what lyf accordyd hym yt wryttē caplm vi y• haue sayd party maye thou vnderstonde whiche one whiche whiche accordyth thy state lyuyng sothly thynketh medled lyf accordeth ye sythen lorde hath ordeyned set ye state souereynte men mekyl lent abundaunce worldly goodes reule susteyne specyally al thise y• vnder thy gouernaunce thy lordship thy myȝt cūnyng also therwith thou receyued grace ye mercy lorde knowe thyself gostly desyre sauour hys loue hope lyfe y• medled best accordeth departe wisly thy lyuyng wyte thou wel yf thou leue nedful besynes actyflyf rekles taken kepe thy worldly goodes spended kept ne makest force thy gettis thyn euen crysten cause desyre wyl y• thou hast yeue gostly occupacyon wenyng yt thou art y• excused yf thou thou dost wysly al thi werkis worth whether bodily gostli done ryghtfully resonably worshyp god bydding sothly ryght noght yf thou leue y• thyng yt thou art bounde ye waye charyte ryght reason wylt holy yeue y• thynge wylfully plesaunce god whiche thou art fully bounde thou dost worshyp discretly hym thou art besy worshyp hed face aray fayr curyously thou leuest body ye foot ragged rent takest kepe therof thou worshypest hym velany worshyp mā curyously arayed vpō hed peyrles precyous stone al body naked bare begger ryȝt gostly worshyp god crowne hed leue body bare thou shalt vnderstonde ye oure lorde ihū cryst man hed gostly body whiche holy chirche y• mēbres body al crysten men som̄ armes foot mēbres sūdry werkynges y• vsen ī lyuing thā yf y• thou besy al thy myght aray hed yt worshyp hymself mynde passion werkes ī manhed deuocōn medytacōn hȳ foryetyst foot yt thy chyldren thy seruaūtis thy tenaūtis al thyn euen crystē letyst hē spyl defaute kepyng vnarayed vnkept tent ouȝt thou plesyst hym thou dost worshyp hym thou makest ye kysse mouth deuocōn gostly prayer thou tredest vpō foot defoulyst hem ī moche thou wylt tent hē neclygence thyselfe y• whiche thou hast take cure thus thynketh neuertheles yf thou thynke yt soth fayr offyce worshyp ye hed hym benial day occupyed medytacyon ye manhed go lower werkys make clene foot besy bothe worde ī dede aboute ye helpe thyn euen crysten thynke sothly wyl thanke ye meke wesshyng foot whan ryght foule stynken vpō ye al ye precyons peyntyng arayeng yt thou canst make hed mynde māhed fayr ynough nedeth bē arayed ye mekyl foot mēbres yt sō tyme euyl arayed nede loked holpen ye nāly sythē thou art boūde therto therfore wyl cūne ye thā ke yf thou wylt mekely tēderly loke hem ye lower seruyce yt thou doost thy lorde ye loue hym ony membres whan nede ryght asketh glad meke herte plesyst thou hym thynkyng yt ynough y• ye lest degre ye lowest state sythen wyl yt semeth sythen hath put ye ī ye state traueyle serue men wel done yt thou sholdee fulfyl thy myght ensample saye thou doost thus say hope yt thou doost thus better wolde thou sholdest thus gladly thynke leue sōtyme gostly occupacōn entermete yt worldly besynes wyse kepyng spendyng thy worldly goodes ī gode reulyng thy seruaūtis thi tenaū ti gode werkis werkyng thyn euen crysten thy myght thou sholdest werkis dyuers tymes gode wyl one thou mygh • est yf thou haddest prayed ben occupyed ghostly thou shalt reteyn tyme breke shalt thou bestly gladly occupy ye bodyly occupacyon thyn euen crysten also whan thou hast ben besy outwarde awhyle thy seruaūtis wich men profitably thou shalt spedful occupacyon outwarde besynes thou sha ••• aye wel occupyed bodyly gostly therfore yf thou wold wel thou shalt gostly iacob dyd bodyly holy wryt sayth yt iacob whan began serue mayster laban coueytyd rachel maysters doughter wyf fayr hed serued seuen yere whan wende haue wyf fyrst lya y• doughte • 〈◊〉 stede rachel afterwarde toke rachel bothe ye last iacob holy wryt vnderstonden ouercomer synnes thyse two wyues vnderstōde saynt gregory sayth two lyues holy chirche actyf lyf contēplatyf lyf lya moche saye traueylous betokeneth actyf lyf rachel moche saye syght begyn̄yng y• god betokeneth lyf contēplatyf lya bare chyl • ren sore yȝed rachel fayre louely barayn ryght iacob coueytyd rachel fayrhed yet nought whan wolde fyrst toke lya afterwarde rachel ryght eche man traueylynge sothfastly conpūccyon grace synnes ye worlde ye flesshe serue god clen̄es gode lyuyng hath grete desyre haue rachel y• haue rest ī gostly swetnes ī deuocōn contēplacyō fayr louely hope haue y• lyf dysposed hym serue oure lorde al myght often whan wende haue rachel y• rest deuocyon lorde suffred hym ben asayed wel tryueyle lya y• eyther tēptacyons ye worlde elles deuyl hys flesshe elles worldly besynes bodyly ghostly helpynge euen crysten whan wel traueyled lya nerhonde onercome lorde yeueth hym rachel yt grace deuocyon rest conscyence hath rachel lya shal thou ensample iacob take two lyues actyf contēplatyf sythen god hath sent ye bothe vse y• one y• • lyf shalt thou bryng forth frute many gode dedes helpe thyn euen crysten yt actyf ye thou shalt made fayre bryght clene souereyn bryghtnes yt god begynner ender al yt made shalt thou sothfastly iacob ouergoer ouercomer al syn̄es grace god thy name shal chaūged iacobs • ame torned isrl israel moche saye man seyng god thē yf thou fyrst iacob dyscretly wylt vse thyse two lyues tyme thou shalt isrl y• contemplatyf eyther thys lyfe yf wyl delyuer make fre fro chargys besyness whiche thou art 〈◊〉 de elles lyf ful blysse heuen whā thou comest thyder man shal desyre contemplatyf fayr medful therfore thou shalt ay haue ī thy mynde thy desyre thou shalt haue vsyng actyf lyf nedeful spedful therfore yf thou put fro reste deuocyon whā thou haddest leuer styl therat eyther thy childrē thy seruaūtis ony thyn euen crysten profyt ese hert skylfully asked angry hem ne heuy ne dredful though god wolde wroth thou leuest hym ony thyng leue lyghtly thy deuocyon whether prayer medytacyon go thy dede thy seruyce thyn euen crysten lyȝtly lorde hymself bad doo suffre mekely loue without grutchyng yf thou mayst dysese trowblyng thyn herte cause medlyng suche besynes ¶ man shall sōtyme haue deuocyon whan hath lettyd outwarde werkys ca vii may fal sōtyme yt ye troublyng y• thou hast outwarde actyf werkis brennyng desyre thou shalt haue god ye clere syght gostly thinges grace oure lorde deuocyon whanne thou comest therto faryth therby yf thou haddest lytyl cole thou woldest make fyre therwith make brenne thou woldest fyrst laye styckis ouerhyle cole styckis neuertheles whan thou hast abyden whyle afterwarde blowest lytyl none shal sprynge oute grete flawme fyre styekis al turned fyre ryght gostly thy wyl thy desyre yt thou hast god lytyl cole fyre thy soule yeueth sōwhat lyght ghostly hete ful lytyl often waryth colde turneth flesshly rest sōtime ydelnes therfore good yt thou putte styckes good werkis actyf lyfe though yt werkes semyth tyme let thy desyre yt may clene ne feruent thou woldest dredful therfore abyde suffre whyle blowe ye fyre yt fyrst goo thy werkis goo thā alone thy prayes medytacyons lyft vp thyn hert god pray hym goodnes yt wyl accepte thy werkes yt thou doost plesaūce holde hē nought thyn owne syght mercy knowe mekely thy wretchydnes thy feelte arecte sothfastly thy gode dedes hym mekyl gode mekyl bad done dyscretly al cyrcūstaunces yt nedeful good dede defaute descrecōn put hē thyself mekenes shal al thy good dedes turne ī flame fyre styckes layde vpō cole shal thy gode dedes outwarde hyndre thy deuocōn rather make ouer lorde sayth holy wryt thus ignis altari meo sēper ardebit et sacerdos surgens mane subiciet ligna vt ignis nō extynguatur fyre shal euer bren myn auter prest rysyng morowe shal put vnder styckes yt quenched fyre loue desyre god soule ye whiche loueth norysshed kept layēg ye stickes yt go thyse styckes douers mater tre som̄ man lettered hath vnderstōdyng holy wryt yf haue fyre deuocyon hert good hym gete hym styckes holy ensāples deuoute prayer norysshe ye fyre hē man vnlettered may redely haue honde holy wrytte ne doctours sayenge therfore nedeth hym many good dedes outwarde euen crysten kyndel fyre loue hem soo good eche man degre dysposed gete hym styckes thynge eyther prayer medytacions redyng holy wryt gode bodyly werkis norysshe ye fyre loue soule quenched affeccyon loue tendre lyghtly wyl vanysshe awaye yf wel kept good dedes bodyly ghostly contynuelly norysshed chanue sythen lorde hath sent thyn herte lytyl sparke blyssed fyre hym selfe holy wrytte saythe ¶dominus noster ignis consumens est ¶ oure lorde god fyer wastynge bodely fyer wasteth al bodyly thyng yt may wasted ryght soo ghostly fyre yt god wastith al maner syn̄e therfore lorde lykned fyer wastyng pray ye norysshe fyer fyer elles loue charyte hath sent ye erthe sayth ī ye gospel ignē veni mittere ī terrā ad quid nisi vt ardeat comē sēde fyre īto ye erth wherto yt sholde brē yt god hath sent fyre loue gode desyre grete wyl plese hym mānes soule vnto ende y• mā shal know kepe noryssh strength therby saued ye desyre yt thou hast hȳ hī ye ye fyre loue ye lesse desyre lesse fyre ye mesure desyre mekyl neyther thyself ony knowest thou ne man god y• yeueth therfore dyspute thyselfe though thou woldest know mekyl thy desyre besy desyre mekyl thou mayst wyte ye mesure desyre ¶what desyre god hymself clennes conscyence cōfort swetnes ca viii saynt austyn sayth yt lyf euery good crysten mā contynuel desyre god grete vertu • grete cryeng ye eres god ye feruentlyer thou desyrest hygher thou cryest ye better thou prayest ye wiselyer thou thynkest desyre sothly thynge butlo thyng al worldes blysse al flesshly lykynge thyn herte wonderful louyng restful yernyng endles blysse heuēly ioy thyng may called desyre god hymself yf thou haue desyre hope sikerly yt thou hast praye y• kepe wel norysshe wysly whan thou shalt pray thynke make desyre begynnyng endyng al thy werke encrece loke none feling ī thy bodyly wittes ne seke none bodyly swetnes neyther sownyng ne sauouryng ne wondfullyȝt ne aūgels syght ne though lorde hymself vnto thy syght wolde apere ye bodely charge lytyl al thy besynes y• thou myȝtest fele sothfastly thy thouȝt lothyng ful forsakyng al maner synne maner vnclennes ghostly syght howe foule vgly paynful thou myghtest haue myghty desyryng vertues meknes charite ye blysse heuen thinketh ghostly comfort ghostly swetnes mannes soule haue celennes ī conscyence fro wyckednes al worldly vynyte stable trouth meke hope ful desyre god euer comfortis swetnessis thynketh swetnes syker sothfast feled clē ne conscyence myghty forsakyng lethyng al syn̄e inwarde syght feruent desyre ghostly thynges al comfortis swetnessys ony maner felynge yf helpe lede ende clennes conscyence ghostly desyre god syker rest askest thou whether desyre loue god vnto saye desyre properly loue begynnyng tastyng loue loue properly ful cowpelynge louer loued togyder god soule one cowpelyng may fully lyf desyre longyng therto ensample man loue mā whiche absent desyreth gretly presence ryght ghostly longe lyf lorde absent fro v yt may neyther se hym ne hym ne fele hym therfore maye haue ye vse thys ful loue ful lykyng may haue desyre grete yernyng present hym se hym blysse fully oned hym loue desyre may haue yefte lyf whiche shall safe loue vnto hym may thus saynt poul sayth ¶scientes qm̄ dū sumus ī hoc corpore pegrinamur dn̄o per fide menim ambulamus non pec sp̄em askest thou may man haue thys desyre herte cōtynuelly y• thynketh nay vnto may saye thynketh yt desyre maye vertu profyt ī hert cōtynuelly werkyng ne vsyng ensāple yf thou seke thou sholdest haue eche mā hath kyndely desyre bodely hele contynuelly ī thyn hert yt thou dedyst whether thou slepe wake aye ylyke yf thou slepe wake thynkest som̄ worldly thynges thou hast thy desyre hert werkyng whā thou thynkest thy bodyly syknes thyn hele thā thou hast ī vsyng ryght gostly desyre god yt hath desyre ye yeft god yf slepe elles thynke god worldly thynges yet hath desyre ī hert ī soule tyl desyre god therfore whan thou doost good dede thynkest god dout thynkyng ī thyn herte whether thou desyrest thy dede sheweth thi desyre vncunnyng wene yt desyre god yf euer cryenge god wordes mouthe erthly ryches thynke dremyng wakynge meanes myght come therto therfore foryeten mynde hēself peynes helle ioyes heuen sothly wy lyke chyldren yt rennē butterflyes loke theyr feete fal somtyme sone downe breken leggis al poupe worshyp worlde ryches iolyte butterflye sothly thyng elli yet mekyl lesse therfore pray ye thou coueytous ye ioyes heuen thou shalt haue worshyp ryches yt euer shal laste haue ryches worshyppes setten nought hem ne setten loue ne lykyng hem lyue euer drede mekenes hope sōtyme sorowe abyden ye mercy god pacyently shal haue fully y• • e coueyted shal crowned kynges stye vp lorde ihū blysse heuen also ben many medytacyons mo saye whiche y• god putteth man̄es mynde styre affeccyon ye reson mannes soule lothe vanytees worlde desyre ioyes heuen thyse wordes saye hadde fully shewed y• maner medytacyons wrought mannes soule touche hē lytyll y• thou myghtest haue vnderstondynge ¶how man shal whan felyth sauour ne comfort medytacyons caplm xv neuertheles thynketh good ye whā thou dysposyst thynke god haue sayd otherwise perauenture thou felyst sauour ne deuocyon thy thynkynge oonly naked mynde weyke wyl yt thou woldest fayne thynke god thou canst hope good yt thou stryue mekyl thyself thou myghtest lyghtly falle derknes yf thou sly thy werkyng therfore holde syker vnto y• saye thy pater noster thyn aue elli thy matynes ellys rede vpon thy sauter y• seuermore syker standarde yt wyl fayle maye cleue therto shal erre yf thou mayst thy prayer gete deuocyon loke deuocyon affeccyon yt saye grete desyre god ghostly delyte holde forth thā thy sayeng breke lyghtly often fallyth yt prayeng ye mouth getyth kepeth deuocyon yf mā cese sayeng deuocyon vanyssheth awaye neuertheles yf deuocyon prayer bryng thyn hert deuout thought manhed lorde ony sayd thought sholde letted thy sayeng thā mayst thoncese thy sayenge occupye medytacyon tyll passe awaye man nedeth • ware ī medytacon caplm xvi certeyn thynges behoneth beware thy medytacyons shal tel ye one whan thou hast gostly thought ymagynacyon manhed lorde suche bodyly thynges thy soule hath ben cō forted fed ther passyth awaye theself besy holde styl maystry turned peyne bytternes also yf passe away dwelle styl thy mynde withouten ony traueyle thyself thou comfort wyl leue therfore reueth thy slepe nyghtes elli ī dayes fro good dedes elles grete feruour thy body thy body thyn hed fallyth gret febylnes shalt thou wylfully breke whā tyme cometh sōtyme whan thou hast deuocion lothest leuen whan passyth resonable tyme ellys turneth dysese thyn enencrysten yf thou thou doost wel thre vntyl hed werke • force cometh hē seldom man yt hath maner werkynge custome eche daye spedful haue dyscrecyon werkyng fully falle therto folowe mekyl wyl comen holde yt good vsen maner deuocion thought hath bē occupyed ymagynacyon manhed lorde ony suche thou art besy al ye desyre thyn herte seke knowyng felyng gost • godhed prese mekyl theron ne suffre thy desyrene thī herte tarye longe
